Therefore, we make them local\n78:     // to the Thread executing the JAR verification code.\n79:     //\n80:     // The code here is used by sun.security.util.SignatureFileVerifier.\n81:     // See there for details.\n82: \n83:     // Hardcoded names of providers to use for JAR verification.\n84:     // MUST NOT be on the bootclasspath and not in signed JAR files.\n85:     private static final String[] jarVerificationProviders = {\n86:         \"SUN\",\n87:         \"SunRsaSign\",\n88:         // Note: when SunEC is in a signed JAR file, it's not signed\n89:         // by EC algorithms. You MUST save the return value from this\n104:      * method, and you MUST call stopJarVerification() with that object\n105:      * once you are done.\n106:      */\n107:     public static Object startJarVerification() {\n108:         ProviderList currentList = getProviderList();\n109:         ProviderList jarList = currentList.getJarList(jarVerificationProviders);\n110:         if (jarList.getProvider(\"SUN\") == null) {\n111:             // add backup provider\n112:             Provider p;\n113:             try {\n114:                 p = new sun.security.provider.VerificationProvider();\n115:             } catch (Exception e) {\n116:                 throw new RuntimeException(\"Missing provider for jar verification\", e);\n117:             }\n118:             ProviderList.add(jarList, p);\n119:         }\n120:         // return the old thread-local provider list, usually null\n121: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/jdk--742e735d@b394eab7f7a9ef928dbbcac1e27e0a0b1577894a/-/blob/src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/Providers.java%3FL1-120"}}}

extends Properties and serves as the base for all security providers. It defines the `putService(Service s)` protected method used by all providers to register their cryptographic services.\\n\\n## Core Built-in Providers\\n\\n1. **SunJCE Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/com/sun/crypto/provider/SunJCE.java): Implements cryptographic algorithms including RSA encryption, DES, Triple DES, AES, Blowfish, ARCFOUR, RC2, PBE, Diffie-Hellman key agreement, HMAC variants, ChaCha20, DHKEM, and ML-KEM. Uses the `putService()` method to register all algorithms through helper methods in the constructor.\\n\\n2. **SunJSSE Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/ssl/SunJSSE.java): The Java Secure Socket Extension provider that registers SSL/TLS factories including KeyManagerFactory, TrustManagerFactory, SSLContext implementations for various TLS versions (TLSv1, TLSv1.1, TLSv1.2, TLSv1.3, DTLSv1.0, DTLSv1.2), and PKCS12 KeyStore implementations.\\n\\n3. **SunEC Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/ec/SunEC.java): Implements elliptic curve cryptography algorithms. Contains an inner ProviderService class that overrides `newInstance()` to create signature, key pair generation, and algorithm parameter implementations for ECDSA variants and EdDSA.\\n\\n4. **Sun Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/provider/Sun.java): The core provider that implements DSA key generation, DSA signing, message digests (SHA-1, MD5), SecureRandom, X.509 certificates, PKCS12/JKS/DKS keystores, PKIX CertPathValidator and CertPathBuilder, and policy/configuration implementations. Uses SunEntries to generate its service list.\\n\\n## Lazy-Loading Infrastructure\\n\\n1. **ProviderConfig** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderConfig.java): Encapsulates configuration for a single provider including the provider name and optional arguments. Implements lazy-loading logic through `doLoadProvider()` method which loads providers on-demand via reflection, using a maximum retry limit of 30 attempts to prevent infinite loops. Maps provider names (module or class names) to actual Provider instances.\\n\\n2. **ProviderList** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderList.java): Manages an immutable ordered list of ProviderConfig entries. Supports operations like `fromSecurityProperties()` to load providers from java.security configuration, and `add()`/`insertAt()` for dynamic provider addition. Uses a dummy EMPTY_PROVIDER during initialization to avoid null checks.\\n\\n3. **Providers** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/Providers.java): Central management class that maintains thread-local and system-wide provider lists. Initializes the default provider list from security properties at static initialization time. Contains the hardcoded list of providers used for JAR verification (SUN, SunRsaSign, SunEC, SunJCE) and provides `getSunProvider()` factory method.\\n\\n## Registration Pattern\\n\\nAll provider implementations follow a consistent pattern: (1) extend the Provider class, (2) call `super()` constructor with provider name and version, (3) register services using `putService(new Provider.Service(...))` where the Service inner class encapsulates the algorithm type, algorithm name, implementation class name, aliases, and attributes. This is demonstrated in SunJCE and SunJSSE through helper methods like `ps()`, and in Sun through SunEntries iterator pattern.\\n\\nThe lazy-loading mechanism via ProviderConfig enables providers to be loaded only when needed, improving startup performance while maintaining transparency to applications through the standard Security API.\"\n}\n"},"caller":{"type":"direct"}}],"stop_reason":null,"stop_sequence":null,"usage":{"input_tokens":11,"cache_creation_input_tokens":1972,"cache_read_input_tokens":84154,"cache_creation":{"ephemeral_5m_input_tokens":0,"ephemeral_1h_input_tokens":1972},"output_tokens":1,"service_tier":"standard","inference_geo":"not_available"},"context_management":null},"parent_tool_use_id":null,"session_id":"f5f4fdef-7899-470f-a82c-1cf39a202576","uuid":"7801445a-2af6-40fa-9abe-5415a51b7016"}

Contains an inner ProviderService class that overrides `newInstance()` to create signature, key pair generation, and algorithm parameter implementations for ECDSA variants and EdDSA.\\n\\n4. **Sun Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/provider/Sun.java): The core provider that implements DSA key generation, DSA signing, message digests (SHA-1, MD5), SecureRandom, X.509 certificates, PKCS12/JKS/DKS keystores, PKIX CertPathValidator and CertPathBuilder, and policy/configuration implementations. Uses SunEntries to generate its service list.\\n\\n## Lazy-Loading Infrastructure\\n\\n1. **ProviderConfig** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderConfig.java): Encapsulates configuration for a single provider including the provider name and optional arguments. Implements lazy-loading logic through `doLoadProvider()` method which loads providers on-demand via reflection, using a maximum retry limit of 30 attempts to prevent infinite loops. Maps provider names (module or class names) to actual Provider instances.\\n\\n2. **ProviderList** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderList.java): Manages an immutable ordered list of ProviderConfig entries. Supports operations like `fromSecurityProperties()` to load providers from java.security configuration, and `add()`/`insertAt()` for dynamic provider addition. Uses a dummy EMPTY_PROVIDER during initialization to avoid null checks.\\n\\n3. **Providers** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/Providers.java): Central management class that maintains thread-local and system-wide provider lists. Initializes the default provider list from security properties at static initialization time. Contains the hardcoded list of providers used for JAR verification (SUN, SunRsaSign, SunEC, SunJCE) and provides `getSunProvider()` factory method.\\n\\n## Registration Pattern\\n\\nAll provider implementations follow a consistent pattern: (1) extend the Provider class, (2) call `super()` constructor with provider name and version, (3) register services using `putService(new Provider.Service(...))` where the Service inner class encapsulates the algorithm type, algorithm name, implementation class name, aliases, and attributes. This is demonstrated in SunJCE and SunJSSE through helper methods like `ps()`, and in Sun through SunEntries iterator pattern.\\n\\nThe lazy-loading mechanism via ProviderConfig enables providers to be loaded only when needed, improving startup performance while maintaining transparency to applications through the standard Security API.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}

Contains the hardcoded list of providers used for JAR verification (SUN, SunRsaSign, SunEC, SunJCE) and provides `getSunProvider()` factory method.\\n\\n## Registration Pattern\\n\\nAll provider implementations follow a consistent pattern: (1) extend the Provider class, (2) call `super()` constructor with provider name and version, (3) register services using `putService(new Provider.Service(...))` where the Service inner class encapsulates the algorithm type, algorithm name, implementation class name, aliases, and attributes. \"src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderList.java\",\n      \"symbol\": \"fromSecurityProperties\"\n    },\n    {\n      \"repo\": \"github.com/sg-evals/jdk--742e735d\",\n      \"path\": \"src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderConfig.java\",\n      \"symbol\": \"doLoadProvider\"\n    }\n  ],\n  \"text\": \"The Java security provider registration framework in openjdk/jdk is built on the following core components:\\n\\n## Base Framework\\n\\nThe foundation is the abstract `Provider` class (src/java.base/share/classes/java/security/Provider.java), which extends Properties and serves as the base for all security providers. It defines the `putService(Service s)` protected method used by all providers to register their cryptographic services.\\n\\n## Core Built-in Providers\\n\\n1. **SunJCE Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/com/sun/crypto/provider/SunJCE.java): Implements cryptographic algorithms including RSA encryption, DES, Triple DES, AES, Blowfish, ARCFOUR, RC2, PBE, Diffie-Hellman key agreement, HMAC variants, ChaCha20, DHKEM, and ML-KEM. Uses the `putService()` method to register all algorithms through helper methods in the constructor.\\n\\n2. **SunJSSE Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/ssl/SunJSSE.java): The Java Secure Socket Extension provider that registers SSL/TLS factories including KeyManagerFactory, TrustManagerFactory, SSLContext implementations for various TLS versions (TLSv1, TLSv1.1, TLSv1.2, TLSv1.3, DTLSv1.0, DTLSv1.2), and PKCS12 KeyStore implementations.\\n\\n3. **SunEC Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/ec/SunEC.java): Implements elliptic curve cryptography algorithms. Contains an inner ProviderService class that overrides `newInstance()` to create signature, key pair generation, and algorithm parameter implementations for ECDSA variants and EdDSA.\\n\\n4. **Sun Provider** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/provider/Sun.java): The core provider that implements DSA key generation, DSA signing, message digests (SHA-1, MD5), SecureRandom, X.509 certificates, PKCS12/JKS/DKS keystores, PKIX CertPathValidator and CertPathBuilder, and policy/configuration implementations. Uses SunEntries to generate its service list.\\n\\n## Lazy-Loading Infrastructure\\n\\n1. **ProviderConfig** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderConfig.java): Encapsulates configuration for a single provider including the provider name and optional arguments. Implements lazy-loading logic through `doLoadProvider()` method which loads providers on-demand via reflection, using a maximum retry limit of 30 attempts to prevent infinite loops. Maps provider names (module or class names) to actual Provider instances.\\n\\n2. **ProviderList** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/ProviderList.java): Manages an immutable ordered list of ProviderConfig entries. Supports operations like `fromSecurityProperties()` to load providers from java.security configuration, and `add()`/`insertAt()` for dynamic provider addition. Uses a dummy EMPTY_PROVIDER during initialization to avoid null checks.\\n\\n3. **Providers** (src/java.base/share/classes/sun/security/jca/Providers.java): Central management class that maintains thread-local and system-wide provider lists. Initializes the default provider list from security properties at static initialization time. Contains the hardcoded list of providers used for JAR verification (SUN, SunRsaSign, SunEC, SunJCE) and provides `getSunProvider()` factory method.\\n\\n## Registration Pattern\\n\\nAll provider implementations follow a consistent pattern: (1) extend the Provider class, (2) call `super()` constructor with provider name and version, (3) register services using `putService(new Provider.Service(...))` where the Service inner class encapsulates the algorithm type, algorithm name, implementation class name, aliases, and attributes.
